<Author>HollyMollyB
<Content>Lovely hotel, perfectly situated After staying nearly a week at the Varenne (in a twin superior room), we echo the vast majority of tripadvisor posts here: it's a wonderful hotel! It's exactly as pictured and described on the hotel website (and in tripadvisor traveler photos), with beautifully decorated rooms, as well as air-conditioning, a refrigerator and safe in the room, and pleasant, helpful people at the front desk. Our room faced the street, yet was very quiet when the windows were closed.The location couldn't be better: within walking distance of a largenumber of tourist sites (Eiffel tower, the Seine, Rue Cler, Invalides + Napoleon's Tomb, Rodin Museum, Place de la Concorde, Pont Alexandre, Champs d'Elysees, Tuileries, etc) yet the immediate surroundings are not touristy; one has the feeling of being in a typical Parisian neighborhood. There was a wonderful boulangerie a couple doors down; also on the same block were a pharmacy, a veg/fruit shop, and a small grocery store. The Paris metro is only 1/2 block away; the RER (railroad, e.g., for trips to Versailles or Vincennes Chateaux or to CDG airport) stop is about 10 min walk. We would definitely stay here again!

<Author>ArtsyGalBaltimore
<Content>Charming Hotel with a Fantastic Location Just returned from a short stay in Paris. I chose the Hotel de Varenne based on positive TripAdvisor reviews and am now adding our own rave review. The location is wonderful, close to two subway stops and a range of museums and sites. The Rodin museum is just around the corner and Napolean's tomb is a brief walk. The Musee d'Orsay is a subway stop away, but we walked it; the Eiffel Tower is also an easy walk. We booked a triple since our teenage son traveled with us and the room was comfortable, a double bed and single bed, and quite spacious for Paris. The room was well furnished, quite tasteful with a stylish French flair, and my son enjoyed the very large flat screen TV. (We didn't bring our laptop, but internet is available and our son was a frequent user.) The bathrooms were spotless and modern. Our third floor room had two windows which overlooked the flowered courtyard. There is a small elevator. The owners were warm and made us feel welcome. The owners kept our luggage for us the day we arrived before check-in and even the day we left--nice touch. We walked each day to Rue Cler for breakfast, and there are local fruit stands and bakeries on the street. Some fine restaurants including La Maupertu are a short walk near Invalides. I would highly recommend this delightful hotel and will definitely stay there when we return to Paris!

<Author>MomandSonMay08
<Content>Thank you Hotel De Varenne! My 20-year-old son and I have just returned from a wonderful stay at the Hotel de Varenne, May 5-May 11. We chose it on the recommendation of friends, and were very pleased. The hotel is in a quiet area and our room overlooked the courtyard, so we were able to sleep with windows open. Our twin room with a shower was very clean, very comfortable, recently renovated, and ample space for our needs. The hotel staff, from first greeting until our departure, was first rate and very helpful. Most of our dealings were with Beatrix and Soultan. Prior to our arrival they arranged reservations for a day-trip to the Normandy and D-Day areas. They assisted with our laptop computer, and arranged for a shuttle back to the airport on the final morning. We chose to have breakfast there each morning, and it was a great start to the day. I ordered the fabulous basket of breads and jellies, juice and a pot of coffee, while my hungry son frequently ordered a la carte to get omelettes or eggs. The metro stop Varenne is very close by, along with a public telephone if you want to use a phone-card. Our most fun experience on the trip was an afternoon tour of Paris by segway, by Fat Bike Tours. Our mom and son trip was a great success, thanks in part to the Hotel de Varenne and staff. I highly recommend it.

<Author>pedlar
<Content>Super location We spent two nights at the Hotel de Varenne. Our room overlooked the small courtyard and was very clean. The double bed was extremely comfortable. The shower was good and powerful with soaps and shampoo provided together with warm towels from the heated towel rail.A flat screen TV with satellite channels completed the facilities.Breakfast was the usual continental with freshly baked baguette, pastries and preserves, fruit juice and tea or coffeee. The down side is the dining room is quite small and can become crowded.The only reason we did not rate as 'excellent' is because we waited 15 minutes sitting at an uncleared table before clearing it ourselves and getting the manager's attention for some service. The previous day we had excellent service so maybe we were just unlucky on this occasion.This hotel is ideally situated for walking to the usual Paris sights, Eiffel Tower, Place de la Concorde, even 'les grands magasins'.As this was our first visit to Paris we took advantage of L'Open Tour, an open top bus tour. We opted for the two day ticket, giving four different tours, to orientate ourselves. Unfortunately, the weather was so cold that we spent the tours inside rather than on the open upper deck. This ticket was good value at 29 Euro as against 26 Euro for a one day pass.We also tried the 'Batobus' a river boat cruise, again with the two day option. This was a very relaxed way to cruise the Seine, in a totally enclosed glass cruise boat.We travelled via Eurostar which was quick and comfortable. Buying a 'carnet' of ten tickets for the Metro was a bit excessive as we only used four because walking and the bus tours were so convenient.We will certainly visit Paris again, and will probably use the same hotel, as the location is ideal.  
<Date>Feb 19, 2008

<Author>Jo_Wicky
<Content>Perfect location, ideal for exploring on foot Just back from a three day stay in Paris at the Hotel de Varenne. The location in my opinion could not be better. Its in a quiet part of the 7th, surrounded by lots of ministerial buildings but its a short walk to St Germain de Pres in one direction and a reasonable walk to the Eiffel Tour in the other direction. We even walked all the way to the Marais via a visit to the Louvre but that was a long walk even by our standards. The hotel itself is a good 3 star standard. Rooms are comfortable although the central heating was a little warm. The most expensive rooms are spacious, the second price level was fine - not a huge size but a nice shower room with separate toilet. On the downside breakfast is not included. My parents paid for breakfast in the hotel one day but were disappointed with quantity and quality. My recommendation is go for a coffee and croissant at one of the lovely cafes around St Germain. Also, this was my first visit to Paris in winter and its a good time to go if you want to visit the museums which are really quiet compared to peak season. And great for the January sales at Gallerie Lafayette and Printemp!For fanstastic posh nosh try restaurant 'Tante Margriette' at the beginning of Rue du Boulongne (where the hotel is) and also visit the lovely wine shop on the same street. The owner is very passionate about wine, very friendly and gave some good tips about the local area.

<Author>Tompell
<Content>De Varenne is a very good hotel - and good value. Hotel De Varenne, Les Invalides, ParisWe stayed for just over a week at this very pleasant family owned hotel. The room and bathroom were lovely, and the services very efficient. The staff went out of their way to be helpful: arranging with us our train travel to Brussels; pointing out metro services (we were en greve at the time - but it worked nevertheless!); and being generally pleasant and helpful without being in anyway overbearing. They provide breakfast - and the coffee and morning breads are just delicious. The hotel is on a quiet sreet with great cafes and restaurants, and a depaneur/boulangerie so you can pick up bread and cheese and a bottle of wine if you don't feel like eating out. They also have a little courtyard - which would be fabulous in the warmer months. Finally the location is great. Just round the corner from the Concorde and really accessible to all one might want to do in Paris - on foot, in order to walk off all that delicious morning bread. We had a lovely time at the Hotel de Varenne.Roberta Ellis and Ken Beeson

<Author>ssoliz
<Content>Great Stay I chose the Hotel de Varenne due to another TripAdvisor review. This hotel is in an area that is populated by foreign ambassador residences and the French Ministry of Defense. <Author>AtlantaVoyager
<Content>Fantastic small hotel My wife and I stayed here for six nights in January 2007 and could not have been happier. We chose the Hotel Varenne based on TripAdvisor reviews, since we did not see it in any guidebooks.The location is fantastic. We were able to walk to the Musee d'Orsay, Saint Germain des Pres, Le Bon Marche, Eiffel Tower, as well as numerous locations on the Right Bank including the Louvre and even the Arc de Triomphe. The neighborhood surrounding the hotel is quite upscale, and is full of bakeries, small markets and other shops that cater to locals, not tourists (which we saw as a plus since we saw the real Paris). Rooms were a tad on the small side, but were very pleasantly decorated, quiet, and very comfortable. The staff was fantastic, and helped with booking restaurant reservations, since our French is lousy. The breakfast in the morning consisted of pastries and breads, and was a wonderful way to start the day.Overall, we really felt at home at the Hotel Varenne, and would definitely stay there again.

<Content>Quaint  We had no idea where to stay when we began planning our trip to Paris. But just in time, our local newspaper published a full-page story on small Paris hotels that were economically priced. <Author>bowlerboy77
<Content>Great Staff at Good, Small Hotel Spent 8 nights at this hotel and must say that the staff is remarkable. Dealt with many of them and everyone was willing to help with any request and never made me feel like I was imposing. In fact, when I had a problem with my room they had the owner/director respond to me personally and his response was courteous, professional and more than satisfactory.If you do want to eat at the hotel I would recommend the a la carte menu for breakfast as a better buy than the continental breakfast.As someone who wants to see the city all day but then be able to sleep at night, this hotel was ideally located in an extremely quiet neighborhood. If you want nightlife, you can find it elsewhere, but come back to the Varenne for a peaceful night's sleep. But if you like to sleep with your windows open as I do, be warned that like most European hotels there are no screens and we did battle mosquitoes a couple of nights.The size of the room was servicable and the bathroom was very big by any standard. The bathroom could have used a little sprucing up; some cracks/peeling in the paint due to the steam from the shower (no shower curtain or enclosure). The housekeeping service was attentive with one exception - had to ask for more soap and shampoo; they weren't replaced as a matter of form.The Paris metro is sensational and the hotel is located very close to the Varenne metro stop. Also an incredibly short walk to the Rodin Museum. We even walked to the Eiffel Tower more than once.As for dining, you can take Rue Grenelle over toward the Eiffel Tower to find several wonderful options starting at Boulevard de la Tour Marbourg and beyond, which we did practically every night.Right on the same street as the hotel, just a few steps away are a bank, small supermarket, fresh fruit stand, bakery, dry cleaner and pharmacy and around the corner is a post office - all your needs are covered.I think it added immensely to stay at this small, boutique style hotel than a major chain. I would recommend the Varenne and would stay there again.

<Content>A Very Special Place I first found this hotel several years ago surfing the web, and booked a room for three nights. From the moment I entered the courtyard, I knew I had discovered something very special. Every aspect of my visit then, and every time I've visited since, has been infused with serenity. The staff is superbly professional and discrete, yet warm and friendly. Beatrix, Bita, Sultan, Valentine, and Mr. Pommier are people that I have come to know and look forward to seeing every year. The rooms are of varying sizes and kept immaculate. The neighborhood is quiet and centrally located to all the sites one comes to Paris to see. After a long day of visiting Paris, it is lovely to come back to Hotel de Varenne and rest in the courtyard or the salon. If you want to keep abreast of the world you left behind, there is an ample supply of daily newspapers, including the International Herald Examiner, or, of course, CNN or BBC World on the flat screen television in your room. Each time I have been to Hotel de Varenne I request, and receive, a room on the First Floor facing the courtyard. I love the large casement windows. When I first went to Paris I was told to stay in a chain hotel, which I did for the first couple of times because I didn't know any better. After having discovered Hotel de Varenne I can't conceive of staying elsewhere. It has become part of the entire Parsian experience for me. As long as Mr. Pommier is the proprietor, and as long as Beatrix is assisting him, I know I will not stay elsewhere. I would recommend to anyone going to Paris to stay at Hotel de Varenne. You will not be disappointed.

<Content>Four years at the Hotel de Varenne! In January, it will have been four years since our first stay at our now- favorite Parisian hotel. We've stayed in every type of room (if not every room, in fact!) and have recommended Hotel de Varenne to many friends over those years. The verdict is unanimous: Hotel de Varenne is a jewel. It is intimate, pretty, friendly, well-appointed without being grand, clean, welcoming, tranquil, and, in spite of the dismally weak American dollar, affordable.We love the de Varenne's location in the 7th arrondissement, on and of the Left Bank, but just a few steps away from the Place de la Concorde, the Tuileries Gardens, and other treasures of the Right Bank.The staff are helpful and kind. Beatrice has become a friend I am always so happy to see when I return to our Parisian home away from home. Soultan is unfailingly polite and helpful. The staff has not changed since our first stay in January 2004, a fact that speaks very well of the hotel management.I stayed here, solo, in early September, in room 41, with its view of the Eiffel Tour (the top half, anyway!) and the hotel's bijoux courtyard. My husband and I are returning for several days in November. And then, it's on to our fifth year at the Hotel de Varenne. You could say we're fans.

<Author>TheSunKing
<Content>A perfect sanctuary in Paris We just spent 8 fantastic days in Paris and stayed at the charming Hotel de Varenne because of the positive reviews on Trip Advisor. The reviews were right on. The staff was great, including multilingual and helpful Beatrix and the night man we called Alfred (cuz he looked like Bruce Wayne's butler).The rooms (Superior) was spacious with a comfortable king size bed, easy WiFi access (12Euro for 24 hrs of on time) and large modern bathrooms with full size bath and shower.The hotel is located in the quiet 7th district. This is mostly government offices so after 5 it is nice and quiet. The Metro is a 5 min walk and Les Invalides is about the same distance.There is a fully stocked mini grocery store across the street and an upscale wine store a little further down. Pastry shops and cafes are nearby.We ended up ignoring the advice to avoid the breakfast and chose to eat in the hotel and get it out of the way. Although the continental breakfast, at 10 Euro, is a bit steep, for 6 euro you could get 2 eggs, coffee and the ever present baguette. Not a bad deal and no leaving the hotel required.The rooms were air conditioned so you can close the windows at night. The windows were all new, so street noise was minimal.And at the end of a long day of looking at wacky French art, make sure you plan to meet in the cozy Varenne courtyard with a bottle of St. Estaphe, a wheel of stinky fromage and yes, a baguette. (and throw a few crumbs to the resident pigeon, who we named Abindicator)All in all, a great, charming hotel at a decent price. We will come back.

<Author>sep1121
<Content>Absolutely Wonderful My girlfriend and I recently spent 6 nights at the Hotel de Varenne, and were very pleased with our pick of hotels. The hotel is on a rather quiet street in a quiet area of the city. This makes it very easy to unwind at night after a long day of exploring the city. The room we had was a standard double with a shower, and it was in very good shape. It was extremely clean and well kept. The bathroom was in excellent shape with a separate WC. The room itself would be considered small for people used to American hotels, but by European standards, it seemed like a standard size room. There was a flat screen TV with quite a few stations, and a DVD player in the TV. However, I don't know why somebody would choose a hotel in Paris based on the TV since it won't be watched much.The hotel is located within a five minute walk to the Invalides, which is where Napolean's tomb is, and about 2 minutes from the Musee de Rodin. There is also a metro station on the same block which made it extremely convenient and easy to get around the city.Most importantly, the staff was wonderful. The staff is who make the hotel what it is. Every staff member was extremely polite and made every effort to help us with whatever we needed. They also served an excellent continental breakfast which jump started our day of sightseeing. I would recommend this hotel to anyone without reservation and would more than likely stay here again.

<Author>ratherbeathome
<Content>Tranquil city hotel Just come back from 6 nights here with my wife and I in a superior double and our 2 boys (11 and 12) in a standard twin. The location has a LOT going for it if you're not used to city (or town for that matter) noise. We live in a rural location with no noise or street light at night, so finding somewhere that we can get a good night's sleep is very important to us and the Varenne certainly does that. The combination of a quiet area, a quiet street within that area and being tucked into a courtyard all help.Check was quick and simple (although I always understood that in customer service protocol it was a good idea to stand up to welcome someone?) and the lift small lift can just about take 2 people and a suitcase. Small but elegant reception area and the whole place has a cared-for feel about it. The hotel's own pics are a good representation of what you'll actually get. Our superior double (room 38) was larger than the boys' twin (25) although the sloping ceiling did mean that a good part of the floor area was either not really usable or could be walked under only with a severe stoop. I lost count of our combined total of head-bumping incidents!Good size and good quality double bed and linens. Very well appointed bathroom and separate WC in both rooms - all immaculately clean and look quite recently installed. Like most hotels they change towels only when you want for 'green' reasons, but sinks don't have plugs so you end up using a lot of extra water unnecessarily. Not quite sure how this fits in to a sustainability agenda?Large flat screen TV in each room - a huge Samsung multi-speaker set up in ours with DVD player too - a big hit with the kids, although it did rather dominate the room.Friendly staff and generous breakfasts served at a leisurely pace (until midday too!) either inside or in the courtyard, or in your room if you want.Location is ideal if you're happy to walk to get around or using the Metro. If you want to be able to stagger back from a heavy night this is not the hotel for you as apart form a small supermarket and shops and 3 or 4 restaurants, there's not much in the immediate area other than embassies and offices. I think the thing we missed most was the ability to get a coffee, tea or cold drink in the hotel other than at breakfast. Most UK rooms have tea and coffee making materials in the rooms and when a hotel doesn't have any bar or room service, and there's nothing in the immediate local area, this is a bit of a drawback.However that's minor niggle comared to everything else about this place and we'd certainly stay there again for a similar holiday.

<Author>WoodstockConnecticut
<Content>We'd Stay Here Again 鈥淢y wife and I just returned from a three week vacation in France. The last three nights were at the Hotel de Varenne. The hotel was perfectly situated for everything we wanted to do in Paris--visit the left bank, the Rodin Museum, the Bon Marche deparment store, and the Orsay Museum. The nearest metro stops (Varenne and Assemblee Nationale) were several blocks away but still conveniently located. We were also in walking distance of some very good restaurants--L'Epi Dupin (near Le Bon Marache), and Florimond (on Ave. de La Motte-Picquet very near Les Invalides). Our room was quite spacious, very clean, air conditioned, and pleasantly decorated. The gentlemen at the front desk couldn't have been more helpful. They helped us with newspapers, taxis, and ordering a shuttle to take us to the airport on the day of our departure. Breakfast in the outdoor courtyard was plentiful but there were other options near by as well. We have stayed in other hotels in Paris in the same appoximate price range but de Varenne is the one we will return to.鈥?br/>

<Author>KimP
<Content>Tranquil retreat Our family of four (including 10- and 13-year-old boys) stayed here for 4 days at the end of June. The hotel does not have connecting rooms, but we had two rooms next to one another at the back of the first (second) floor and felt as if we had our own little wing. As other reviewers have described, the rooms were spacious by European standards, nicely decorated, comfortable beds and linens, nice bathrooms. Couldn't have asked for more in that regard. Our rooms overlooked the lovely courtyard, which was very tranquil. A nice place to peruse your guidebooks while having a late afternoon wine and cheese break, as I observed one couple doing. We did notice that, because of the courtyard's enclosed nature, sound traveled quite easily up from the courtyard as well as from room to room. (For instance, with the windows open, we could hear our kids talking in their room next door.) However, during our stay, the hotel was very quiet (except for my family!) and we were never bothered by outside noise.Based on reviews here and elsewhere, we chose this hotel for our first stay in Paris because it was important to us to have a quiet place to return to at the end of a day out in the city. We got what we wished for--almost too much so! We arrived on a Saturday and the neighborhood was nearly deserted for the weekend. We had trouble finding open restaurants nearby on both Saturday and Sunday nights. Once Monday came around, it was like a different place, as the neighborhood is home to many government offices. There are grocers, patisseries, and fruit markets along the street, selling delicious (and expensive!) treats. The neighborhood is pleasant to walk around, but if you are looking for a lively neighborhood, with lots of street life, this is probably not the best location in which to base yourself.Once inside the hotel, all is quiet. I know that most people would find this very pleasant (and I'm not complaining!), but as a family travelling with two not-always-quiet boys, we sometimes found it a bit oppressive. Even at breakfast, guests seemed inclined to speak in hushed tones. So, just a warning that it might not be the best option for anyone travelling with young children.Recent reviews here have mentioned the helpful staff, but I'm sad to say that we did not find this to be the case. This is my one main complaint with the hotel and would be a serious consideration in whether I would ever stay here again. One of the reasons we decided to stay in a hotel during our first trip to Paris, rather than to rent an apartment, was because we wanted to be able to get information on local restaurants, the Metro system, shops, etc. Of the 4 or 5 desk staff we dealt with during our stay, only one could be considered friendly and somewhat helpful. When we were having trouble finding restaurants open on the weekend, and we specifically asked the man at the desk for suggestions, he just motioned with his hand that there were many restaurants over that way. This may not be the best place to stay if you are in Paris for the first time and are hoping to get advice from the staff about things to see and do. In the lobby, I didn't notice any maps or literature around for tourists. Though there were many tourists, mostly American, at the hotel during our stay, I had the impression that the hotel sees itself more as catering towards those who are on business in the area.Lastly, the subject all reviews must deal with: the breakfast! We chose to have breakfast at the hotel each day; it was just easier for us. People complain about paying 10 Euros but, unless you really are only going to buy a cup of coffee and a croissant, in that neighborhood, you really aren't going to save any money. You will save time, however! The breakfast room is small and we had to wait about 10 minutes one day for a table to open up. Even when we were the only ones in the room, service was quite leisurely, so don't expect a quick bite and a gulp and go! There is a standard continental breakfast, but also a junior version (6 Euros), and many a la carte options, including eggs. No complaints with the food; it was very tasty and more than ample. And you can walk a few doors down for the most delicious fruit to accompany your breakfast! For the jetlag set, another plus is that breakfast is available until midday, which we gratefully took advantage of the first morning of our arrival.This is a lovely hotel, as many reviews have noted. We wanted a quiet place, and that's what we got. My only complaint would be the less-than-friendly staff.

<Author>SoCalFamily4
<Content>Quiet, Convenient Location Our family of four, including two teenage daughters, just returned from a 8 night stay at the Varenne. The hotel is on a quiet street which is convenient to many sites and the metro. We booked two rooms (a double and a twin bed) facing the courtyard. The double was small, but perfectly adequate for our two daughters.We did not eat breakfast at the hotel as we thought 10 Euros per person was a bit high, so we picked up pastries at one of the excellent bakeries on the street. We appreciated having a refrigerator in our room to store water, drinks, etc. which we purchased from the store across the street.The only downside to the hotel is the fact that it IS in a very quiet location with many government buildings. On our next trip, we would probably stay in an area like the Marais which is a bit livelier, and which has more restaurants and activities.

<Author>mars000210
<Content>Elegant Hello,we just got back from our trip to Paris and thought I would post on the two hotels we stayed at while there.This hotel was located in the district where the embassies are located. ON a narrow street boarded by large embassy complex's and Rouden Museum just up the street the invalides park just two blocks away. Charming area, very quiet. A long narrow street, boarded by small shops and including two small mom and pop grocery stores.The room we booked was on the 2nd floor. It was large and the window opened on to a view of other ( we assumed homes) not a bad view at all. the room was largest of the two hotels in Paris we lodged at and the 2nd largest of the three hotels for our whole trip. The bathroom was large and had lovely tile and amenities the shower was thought not large was roomy enough with a shower curtain closure. Soaps and Shampoos were better quality then at the other hotels, large towels of nice quality and in the winter the towel rack must be designed to heat the towels up, nice touch. The whole bathroom was tiled, it was elegant looking.The room had besides nice furnishings, a thin, mounted TV, with cable with two channels for those that miss their CNN or BBC, English speaking TV. Adequate hair dryer in the bathroom. A safe, and a refrigerator as well. The closet lighted up the interior when it was opened and had shelf's and room to hang clothing. There was also a stand to place ones luggage on, rather then have ones bags on the floor.The bedding covers were nice, as were the linens for the bed and mattress and pillows were comfortable. all matched the decor nicely.When you enter the hotel it has a garden entrance with small table to sit at and read or eat a snack, or write home. The hotel had breakfast , the usual fair for Paris hotels, but we skipped that to eat at the local bakeries and restaurants. The other guests ate breakfast and the food appeared to look good. The first floor contained the lobby which was quaint and a breakfast eating area. The lift goes to the upper levels and well as there is a carpeted stairs to the upper floors.We had one hot day on our trip , and we were at this hotel and the air conditioner worked well. Individual units for each room. So you could adjust the air to ones choosing. It was quiet area, we enjoyed our stay there and would go again. \for those that are disabled it would be a good choice as there is space for either a wheel chair or electric wheel chair to be stored and no stairs to climb, and the larger rooms size and bathroom would be plus.The staff were nice and helpful, but not as friendly as the first hotel we used, I would say they were more gracious in manner when helping the guests. Not snooty, just more reserved in manner. Always a smile. It was some what a little more elegant place, compared to our other hotel. I was told they accommodate many visitors that have business at the embassies near by, that might account for the more reserved tone of the hotel, but don't get me wrong, the staff was still very nice.It is still a thumbs up choice. The walk to the Eiffel tower , about 2 miles in distance.The Museum D'Orsay was also close, about the same distance. There are several restaurants several blocks over with outside dining .In all we were glad we had two slightly different experiences with the hotels we chose, This hotel was a good choice to bring back some fond memories of Paris.I know many say you don't go to Paris to see the room, but to wake up and go to bed at night or take a break during the day for us it was nice to have a little ambiance of Paris in our commendations as well. I hope someone finds this helpful when making their choice when going to Paris.As I found the reviews here on tripadvisor a real plus when making our choices as to where to stay.Barbie

<Author>Jacana
<Content>Great location We booked the Hotel de Varenne based on the Trip Advisor reviews. We used the RER to get there (Line B from CDG changing to Line C at St. Michel toward Invalides). This cost us 6.8 Euro apiece. Then it was about a 5 block walk to the hotel. This worked for us because we had carry on rolling luggage only but it wouldn't work for people with more luggage or those who couldn't walk well. You could take a taxi from Invalides if you wanted to but it would still be difficult to navigate through the train stations if you had a lot of luggage. We opted for the shuttle for the return trip as we had an early morning flight. Francesca at the desk arranged this (34 Euro for both of us) and then we asked her to confirm it the evening before. That worked out very well and we were at the airport in plenty of time. Actually we had excess time since Air France was late as usual.When we arrived at the hotel we were able to check in early which was very nice since we had come in from an all night flight. We had been confirmed with a courtyard view room but we were given a street view room. When I pointed this out to Francesca, she said there had evidently been a mix up and said there were no courtyard rooms that evening but there would be the next two evenings and that she would move us. She did move us to a higher floor with a street view room which was fine and we decided that it wasn't worth moving the next night to the courtyard room because there was very little noise from the street.One of the best things about this hotel is the location. It is on a very quiet street which is convenient to many sites, the Batobus, shops and the metro. The only downside we found as far as the location was that many of the restaurants were closed on the weekends. We ate at the Japanese restaurant down the street twice which was very good and reasonable in price. We at the restaufant Tante Marguerite the first night and I would not recommend it...it was very expensive with mediocre food with small portions. We ate breakfast at the hotel the first morning for 10 euro each. We thought this was a little high for a couple of croissants and bread and tea, chocolate or coffee but it tasted fine and was convenient. The other two mornings we bought our own pastries at a bakery down the street.We really liked it that the hotel was in a quiet area (near government buildings). It felt very safe and since there were big crowds everywhere else we went, it was nice to have someplace to go that wasn't full of people.The staff was very helpful and friendly and I would recommend it for a stay in Paris.  
<Date>May 3, 2007

<Author>CAL_NORTH
<Content>Great location The hotel is in an excellent location. Nice and quiet and much more calm than the Latin quarter we usually stay in. It does take some transferring on the Metro and RER to get almost anywhere if that is your means of transit. This could be a problem if you are coming from the airport with bags as many stations only have stairs.The staff is friendly and helpful although do not expect a concierge who can make suggestions and book dining and site seeing. They do speak English and will call for you if you do the research first. There are many restaurants and cafes in the area so we never opted for breakfast in the hotel. It is also located walking distance from Rue du Bac where there is an excellent up-scale modern food store. Also there is Ryst Dupeyron, the best Armagnac shop in Paris where you can taste many old vintages and ports. The rooms do have small refrigerators which was nice especially for keeping that cheese and water cold. There is a small courtyard with chairs and tables at the hotel entry which we used to have our wine and cheese.Be prepared that each room has a heating/cooling unit mounted high on the wall in a corner. They mounted the controls under the unit so you have to get on a chair to make adjustments - which is problematic especially in the dark if you want to change the settings. There are also no instructions as to how to use the controls so you may want to ask.All in all I would stay there again.

<Author>FLEABUS
<Content>Perfect for average Paris tourist Stayed here for 5 nights in Aug 2005. This place is 3 star and perfect for what the average tourist needs who wants to retire at the end of the day to peace and quiet. It is situated in the Government district of the city which is not only quiet at night but also full of fine buildings. Eiffel Tower is only a short walk away too. I would recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Author>AnNorth
<Content>Quiet haven in Paris My mother and I stayed in Hotel de Varenne just before Christmas 2006. We wanted a hotel in a quiet and safe area, within walking distance of the city centre (St German des Pres etc.), and not too expensive.Hotel de Varenne proved to be just that. We booked the winter special offer (129 euro per room, breakfast included) and for that price, we got an authentic, nicely furnitured and comfortable place to stay; a quiet haven from the moment you walk into the entrance garden.Initially, we had a room on the fourth floor based on our miscommunication, but the staff was more than helpful to transfer us to the second floor; less stair-climbing and somewhat spacier.Considering the price, the room was good: nice furniture, excellent badroom and well ventilated. Not much view since we booked a room on the courtyard, but we had absolutely no traffic noise at night. Only the polyester blankets we considered out of date and not too clean, but this was not a great problem.Breakfast is (like in almost every hotel of this pricerange) typically French: tea, coffee or chocolate, orange juice and a basket of bread. If you don't expect an English hotel breakfast buffet, then it's all very fine.The hotel lies in the eastern part of the 7th Arrondissement, a very safe and well-heeled neigbourhood, with some nice restaurants quite nearby. We particularly recommend Le Ferme de Saint Simon (in the Rue de St Simon), a lovely restaurant with very kind staff, however somewhat expensive.Even late at night, this area is very safe, also for two women alone. You can walk to St Germain des Pres (twenty minutes) or to the city centre via the Tuileries (half an hour). There are also two metro stations nearby. If you want a quiet place to stay in a authentic, charming hotel on a moderate budget, Hotel de Varenne is just the right place to you.  
<Date>Dec 25, 2006

<Author>themoos
<Content>Best value for your Euro We had stayed at the Varenne 10 years ago, and were so pleased to find it even better than before. The decor is pleasant, the rooms are smallish but comfortable and clean as a whistle, baths up to date, but most of all the location is perfect. Centrally located at the edge of the 7th arr., easy walking distance to the Musee d'Orsay, the Rodin Museum, the Invalides, Grand Palais etc. etc. Close to a metro station. Most of all, the concierge/receptionist, Beatrix, is a gem. Multi lingual, very helpful, went out of her way to anticipate our needs, helped us find locations with a map of the city, lent us guidebooks, suggested restaurants and booked for us - all with a smile. We believe that the Varenne must be one of the best values for the money in Paris, an expensive city. We have recommended it to friends, and certainly would stay there again ourselves.

<Author>generaltravel
<Content>Nice hotel, a few glitches... My husband and I stayed at Hotel de Varenne for 8 nights. It was quiet and quaint. The courtyard is lovely and we enjoyed our breakfast there in the morning. The room was more spacious than anticipated, but cleanliness was not top grade. There was so much dust on the dark red lamp cover, I drew happy faces on it to get the cleaner's attention. The happy faces remained untouched for our entire stay. The DVD player came with the room, great free selection of movies too! but the DVD player turned out to be broken and didn't get fixed when brought to the attention of hotel staff. FInally, our flight got bumped to 8:30 am (instead of noon) and we let the manager know we would have to take a hotel room at the airport on the last night because we had to be there early and we were 1 hour away by metro. He told us that we had reserved the room and we would have to pay for it. We emphasized to him that we didn't want to leave, our flight time was changed, we had been there for 7 nights and it was 9:00 am - way before the checkout time, and we wouldn't be there for the breakfast which was included in our price. He suggested we take a taxi (about 100 E) instead of the metro (14 E for 2 people) and again stated he would charge us for the room that night regardless. We thought this was inconsiderate and insensitive. In the end, we called the airline, paid for advanced flight booking and woke up at 5:00 am to get to the airport by metro at 5:30. Overall though, we do recommend this hotel to others. It is charming and ideally located for sightseeing; just make sure you don't have a change in plans!

<Author>dmmbmom
<Content>Inexpensive, quiet, perfect If you don't need or want the expense of fancy lobbies, huge chandeliers, etc., then this is perfect. I stayed there with my four kids (ages 10 - 17) for a week. It's a small hotel; the lobby is about the size of a bedroom and the dining room is even smaller. But it's right around the corner from the terrific Musee Rodin (sculptor of The Thinker, The Kiss, etc.), and within walking distance of Les Invalides, the Eiffel Tower, and the Rue Cler. My kids and I also walked from the hotel to places like St. Germain des Pres, St Michel (Notre Dame area), Place de la Concorde, Champs-Elysees...pretty much all the main tourist attractions are within a half-hour of walking, which is not much by Parisian standards.Comfort-wise the main things are that it has good air-conditioning in the bedrooms, the bathrooms are clean and updated and have great smooth Corian sinks (I wanted to take one home!). Like most European hotel rooms, the ones at the Hotel de Varenne are small by American standards, but the 5 of us were perfectly comfortable in two rooms. The staff is helpful and pleasant. A woman named Beatrix was particularly nice to me and my kids and gave us suggestions on where to go. The morning breakfast is included in the room rate and is the typical delicious hotel continental breakfast fare. I got very used to hot chocolate and croissants being served to me on pretty yellow and blue-flowered china.I would definitely recommend this place.

<Author>Maribri
<Content>Spotless, Comfortable  We had 5 nights at Hotel de Varenne and we loved it. We booked a basic double room with shower and it was more than adequate. The bed was very comfortable and the bathroom excellent. The staff are helpful and speak excellent English and breakfast is very good. Our Paris stay was at the end of a long holiday and after splashing out on dinner at the Moulin Rouge (absolutely fantastic and worth every cent) we were on a budget. The restaurants right by the hotel looked excellent but were quite expensive when converted to Australian dollars. However, a supermarket is across the road and we had delightful picnic dinners which suited us better. We have already recommended this hotel to friends visiting Paris and we will stay there again. It is very close to a Metro and we were able to access everything easily. A good, solid choice.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great value hotel We stayed at the Hotel de Varenne largely as a result of the reviews posted on this site, and I have to add that the reviews were accurate: this is an excellent hotel in a convenient location which, by Parisian standards, offers good value for money.The location is close to several of the French ministries, and is not on a main street, so is relatively quiet. The street is well served with restaurants, a small supermarket and a patissserie.The standard of cleanliness is very high throughout the hotel and, as it has recently been renovated, is also well and tastefully decorated.We stayed in room 17 (147 euros a night), which overlooked the small garden, and were pleased with the size of the room and the bathroom - it was not cramped at all. The rooms all have flat screen tv with 3 English-speaking news channels, a safe and small refrigerator. Bathrooms are equipped with a hairdryer and basic toiletries. Contrary to another report, it is possible to adjust the air conditioning.The staff were helpful and friendly, and all seemed to enjoy working in the hotel. However, we did request a taxi to be called for 8.30 am, to take us to the airport, but the staff did not call the day before, as asked, and the staff on the desk in the morning had a great deal of difficulty in locating a vehicle during rush hour.Breakfast was a resonable deal, but could be had cheaper at a local patisserie. The meal consists of tea/coffee, fruit juice, and an assorted basket of mini croissants, baguette and pains au chocolat/pains aux raisins. It is certainly sufficient for any adult with a healthy appetite. A la carte items such as cereal can also be requested at a modest price.I would not hesitate to return, or to recommend the hotel to others.

<Author>JRM22
<Content>We loved the Hotel de Varenne My husband and I just returned from a 10 day vacation in Paris. We stayed at the Hotel de Varenne in the 7er. We absolutely fell in love with the neighborhood and this little jewel of a hotel. Just as you have read in the othe reviews and forums here, Rue De Bourgogne has everything you need for your stay. A Patisserie next door -- delicious Quiche! -- an ATM, pharmacy, grocery stores, wine shop, book store and a couple of small restaurants are on this street. Assemblee Nationale is located at one end of the street and the Musee Rodin is at the other (across the street) so the area is very safe. There are two Metro stations nearby.We arrived at the hotel around 10:00 am and were delighted to find our room was ready for us. The room was small but very nicely decorated in provencial colors, very clean and comfortable. The bathroom was large with a tub and shower, a nice vanity and a separate water closet. We had very little noise because our room overlooked the courtyard. We stayed in Room 25.Beatrix and Soultan, hotel staff, were very courteous and helpful. Our luggage did not arrive with us (good ole United Airlines) and Beatrix and Soultan went out of their way to assist us in locating it. Beatrix also made arrangements for our side trip to Brugge, Belgium and she and Soultan arranged for taxis a couple of times. We made our request the night before and yes, they were there on time! We enjoyed the lovely courtyard area. It was a relaxing place to have a glass of wine after a long day of sightseeing. A couple of nights we just picked up something to eat and had dinner in the courtyard. Afterwards, we walked a couple of blocks to get a view of the Eiffel Tower light show. We are looking forward to our next trip to Paris and will definitely stay on the left bank at the Hotel de Varenne.

<Author>Alyssia
<Content>A nice hotel My husband and I stayed at Hotel de Varenne for 5 nights while we were in Paris. We picked this hotel based on the review here. We were in room 43 which looked over the front of the building. The room was the typical small room and very clean. We thought the hotel was in a very good location, and close to the metro; which made getting around very easy. The staff was friendly, and helped us when we had questions. We did feel that breakfast was not worth the cost here. For 10 euro, you would get a small basket of assorted breads, coffee and Juice. If you're looking to save a little cash, 2 doors down from the hotel, there is a great bakery and across the street from that is a nice grocery store. Since the room offered mini- refreg, we bought water, cheese, lunch meat and stuff for our bread that we got at the bakery and had that for breakfast.If we were to go to Paris again, I would probably consider this hotel again.

<Author>TripAdvMember12
<Content>Decent stay We just returned from a 3 night stay at this hotel, selected primarily on the basis of the reviews posted here and price (naturally). I felt it was a decent spot but not as good as the reviews have made it out to be. Our room was not available at 12:15 PM so we had to leave our bags and have lunch at a creperie down rue de Bourgogne (which was lovely, by the way). We came back an hour later and were given our key. The room was quite small (which we weren't surprised about) but relatively clean. Not that well lit, and the bathroom was very strange as it had built-in shelves that seemed very gratuitous. There was a flat screen TV and DVD player which was a nice touch, as well as a mini-fridge. Our bed was a not very comfortable double.As other reviewers have noted, the staff is not particularly helpful as far as restaurants although they did give my husband a little map of the area with marked places on it. They also helped him find a place to get some takeout soup for me as I was ill. Also they did not replace our soap or even the plastic cups used for water after I threw them away one night, which I think is a pretty basic thing to expect.The other frustrating thing about the location is that although you are nearly close enough to the Hotel des Invalides metro stop, the closest one is actually the Varennes stop, which is not on a major line. We did a lot of transferring to get to this line, although to be fair, you really could just walk most of the time. We walked from the hotel to St. Germain de Pres and the Eiffel Tower, although they might be far for some people. To summarize I would say it was a decent stay although I wouldn't be likely to seek it out again - will probably try another similarly priced, better located three star and see how we make out.

<Author>RCGCanada
<Content>Nice Paris Hotel We stayed at Hotel de Varenne after reading reviews on Trip Advisor. We very satisfied with the hotel and would stay there again as a fall back should we not find something better.Location: Metro station is fairly close. Varenne is on the opposite side of the block, so it鈥檚 a 6 or 7 minute walk to the entrance. The hotel is located on a fairly quiet street 鈥?minus garbage day and when the police go whizzing by. We did notice a fair amount of foot traffic, yet felt very safe. Nearest shops and bars are located all along the street of the hotel. Great food shops and a pharmacy just down the street. The last little grocer closed at 22:30.Overview: The hotel is an older building with a clean and tasteful d茅cor. One enters the hotel via a garden which is set up with tables. Breakfast can be eaten here 鈥?it was a 10 euro option we declined. The lobby has a computer with internet accesses, available for 4 euros for 30 minutes.Staff: The staff at check in was friendly and helpful. There is only 1 person working the small front desk. You interact with them a lot since you must leave your room key behind each time you leave the hotel.Rooms: Small by North American standards, yet reasonable. Furnished with the same tasteful look as the lobby. The room included a small TV with basic mulit-lingual channels (3 in English, BBC/CNN/SKY), there was a safe and a mini fridge. Air conditioning was centrally controlled, so you had no input into the room temperature. Noise: Hotel is older, and you can hear the other guests closing doors and any other loud noises. The street can be noisy with Police and garbage trucks. Bed: We found it reasonably comfortable, however it was a double so small by our standards.Bathroom: Clean, yet small. Only had a shower which has moderate water pressure and a steady stream of hot water.Overall, we would recommend this hotel. The location is fantastic, however the noise is a turn off.

<Author>brooklynwanderers
<Content>Great Value with shortcomings We stayed 9 days/nights at this hotel in mid-May 2006. We read all the reviews before choosing the hotel, and found most all the reviews were very accurate, though I have a different take on some aspects of the hotel and neighborhood. The value is very good for such a clean hotel with new bathrooms, in a nice neighborhood. But our room (the cheapest rate room offered, with a shower not a tub) was TINY and we felt b/c we were staying and paying for 9 nights they could have given us a larger room for the money. It's difficult not even having a chest of drawers and having to literally live out of the suitcase for 9 days. I love the 7th arrondissment. It's so close to many sites, and it's clean and picturesque. Musee Rodin is a couple blocks away which all our friends urged us to see and which was wonderful having nearby b/c we got to see it twice, once in the day and once late at night after dinner. The real difference between the pricier hotels and this one is the staff, ultimately. Only very self-sufficient and people who already know Paris should stay here because the staff know almost nothing about restaurants to recommend, how and where to get a cab for dinner (though they will phone for an airport shuttle for you) or what stores sell what nearby. They are all friendly people, but do not provide true, proper concierge service. We actually had to walk to another more expensive hotel our first night, to get a recommendation from that concierge for dinner who more readily helped us even though we weren't guests there. Also note the nearby restaurants (many good ones, btw) close early and keep odd hours on odd days, so if you need to eat dinner late plan to eat in another neighborhood or to buy sandwiches you can carry back to the hotel. Otherwise you'll be left digging for stray lefotver airline peanuts in your purse like I was one night! But don't be scared off by my comments, it's a great hotel and a great value. Just keep these tips in mind, and splurge for the room with bath which is significantly larger than the room with shower. Bon Voyage!

<Author>Planestrainsnautos
<Content>Great value in Paris My wife and I just returned from Paris where we spent 8 nights in Room 26, a standard double which looked out over the courtyard. Rate 146E. I researched the Parisian hotels extensively prior to booking. Try to find a 3 star hotel at this rate in a fairly central location where the rooms and bathrooms are relatively large, well decorated and clean, and come with a small refrigerator (great for storing wine and picnic items), an in room safe, a flat screen TV with 3 english speaking channels, and a shower curtain. There was no alarm clock but you can program the phone to give you a wake up call. I'd bring an alarm clock for back up though. The room was very quiet with respect to outside noise. But the walls are apparently pretty thin. The phone in the adjacent room was easily heard in ours. That said, we rarely heard any voices. I think everyone must have spoken in quiet tones. The prior reviewers were dead on with respect to the location of the hotel. For those wanting to walk out of the hotel into a street of action, stay elsewhere. Such a street is a good 15 minute walk or so. Nevertheless, there are plenty of restaurants, a grocery store and everything else you'll need very close by. ATM is just down the street. The nearest metro is an easy 5 minute walk. Most of the top attactions are within a 15-30 minute walk.The staff was for the most part reserved but very helpful. This is not a BB type place where they fall over themselves to help you but I believe that's the norm for Paris. There are about 6 people who staff the front desk 24/7. Not all had restaurant recommendations. They give you a xerox copy of a map showing some French restaurants in the 7th but they don't seem prepared to make other recommendations, which is probably not unusual. So come prepared with your own list of places to eat. They will gladly make reservations, call cabs and do all that stuff. For you Mastercard holders, you might check with the hotel to confirm that they take it. We tried to pay for our stay with one and it was not accepted. The receptionist didn't know why but said it was a problem on her end which was clearly the case since I'd been using that card all week, had notified my MC company we'd be in Paris, had gobs of money left on the credit limit, and were able to use it immediately when we got home. So I'm not sure what the problem was. Fortunately we had a Visa card which did go through.We would not hesitate to stay here again.

<Author>hw409
<Content>Great hotel Just got back from staying here last week, and miss it already heh. Really nice hotel - while it isn't cheap per se (many of the rooms approach or exceed $200), you get what you pay for and I think it was a good value for the quality. Impeccable rooms in nice matching Empire furnishings along with flat screen TV, DVD player, and free movies. The staff was reserved but helpful; a good match for the generally well-heeled clientele. Location is good. A nice number of cafes, patisseries, and small groceries right on the street, but of course it isn't the Latin Quarter either. Lots of small fancy businesses, embassies, etc. so basically lots of people in suits during the day. These stores all close at night too, but the area is very safe at night and you're just a 10 minute walk to the Rue Cler area. About 5-10 min walk to the Metro. The nearest Metro stop (Varenne) is not on a main line, so some switching will be necessary if you're planning on taking it to most other areas. The location is perfect is you're planning on concentrating in the Champs-Elysees, Invalides, Eiffel Tower, Rue Cler area, or if you've seen most of the high-volume tourist areas near the Notre Dame already.Basically the hotel was so nice it made us want to stay in it longer during the day, which for jet-lagged travelers could be a dangerous thing! (By contrast, our first (and much cheaper) hotel in the 6eme was so small you always felt compelled to leave) Highly recommended, for those who aren't set in staying in the more high-traffic areas.

This hotel definitely deserves its rank.My only trepidation in writing this review is that someday it will be too popular to get a reservation! After comparing its location with my other top choices, I'm glad we choose it. The laws of physics dictate that if it's a busy street and you're above it, noise travels up! at first glance the street did look very quiet, but as we got to know the area we found all we needed. Others have mentioned the various shops for food, etc..so I'll just mention the ATM at the end of the block (left out of the hotel) where you feel very safe. We ate at Le Basilac, one of the restaurants on the sheet that the front desk will give you for asking. It's very close and business was just picking up when we left at 9p.m.We loved the hotel! The staff is gracious, polite and willing to help. The rooms are clean and tastefully decorated and the bathrooms were great. My husband is a pretty good-sized guy and he felt very comfortable with the beds and the bath. The mini-fridge came in handy and we stocked up from the store across the street (and the patiserrie down the street)We ordered a taxi for the airport the day before with the front desk and it arrived right on time.The gentleman that placed the order was kind enough to ask about our luggage and realize we would need to reserve a larger taxi.Oh,just remember that if you order a taxi, the meter starts from their departure point, not your's!We're definitely going to stay here again.t

<Author>melodyMD
<Content>Perfect hotel-Totally DEAD location This hotel is perfect for anyone who wants nothing more than peace, quiet and luxury from a hotel in Paris. But, if you want a lively neighborhood, a feel for real Paris charm and life - you won鈥檛 want to stay here and for this one reason, I personally would never stay at this hotel again. I just wish I could move it to a more interesting neighborhood. The location is perfect for those who prefer a very quiet in a rather ritzy neighborhood in Paris. This hotel is in the area of governmental buildings and embassies, on a street which has one or two restaurants, and a few businesses, mostly high-end specialty shops and very few places of interest in general 鈥?and it was dead, day or night. The neighborhood seems very reserved and uppity. The plus side is that it makes it super safe, but at night, its like a nuclear bomb has hit after 9 pm. Nothing is open and everything is deadly quiet- you are lucky if you see another human in the vicinity of the hotel after 10 pm. God forbid you need a meal after 9 pm in this area.... This may have been due to the season (Late March-early April) but somehow I got the feeling this was typical of the street all year round. As I much prefer a lively neighborhood with businesses that stay open late, I鈥檇 choose to stay in another area, such as Rue Daguerre in Montparnasse 鈥搚ou get a truly feel for Paris 鈥?the local groceries stay open till 3 am and people sit around chatting and drinking in cafes until well after midnight鈥?its a nice break from the over-lively and touristy St. Germain areas and has a number of nice hotels. If I could move Varenne to such an area, it would be perfection in Paris.If you are the type who likes to retreat to a super quiet residential area at night, look no further. There is nothing more you can ask for in a hotel in Paris in this price range and there is a reason why this is #1 on tripadvisor in its price group. The hotel is super clean, with the best quality material used for every part of it 鈥?from the windows, which are new and double glass for quiet, to the plasma TVs, DVD players, luxury bathroom with great shower and water pressure 鈥?you won鈥檛 find better quality at some 4* places in Paris. Everything is super clean. Skip the breakfast and go to another neighborhood for breakfast (because you won鈥檛 get any options here other than the Patisserie next door, which is pricey) 鈥ut other than that, everything about the actual hotel is fantastic. All you have to do is be the type who likes it totally dead in the neighborhood you stay, and thinks of the hotel as a place of rest and nothing else.

<Author>Havlat
<Content>A Good Hotel We stayed at the Hotel de Varenne mid-March for 7 nights. We did a lot of research on Paris hotels prior to our trip and found that the Varenne is an excellent value compared to other hotels in Paris. The hotel is on a quiet street, but very centrally located to many sites in the city. My one complaint with the location is the lack of restaurants in the immediate area, after a long day of walking around the city it would have been nice to have some options close to the hotel. There is an excellent bakery next door, a grocery across the street, and two bank machines at the rue de Grenelle and Bourgogne. The area is very safe and we felt very comfortable walking around late at night. The hotel: the lobby is very small, with a small dining area to the right as you enter. We never ate breakfast at the hotel, but was usually busy when we were leaving in the morning. A very small elevator was tucked away at the other side. The lobby was very small but quaint. We stayed in two different rooms during the week. The first was priced at 120 euros and was located on the second floor. It was located at the end of the hallway, which I thought would be great for noise, but the walls were extremely thin. We heard every noise made in the room next to us, below us and above us, usually sound doesn't bother me, but it was pretty bad...some nights we had a hard time sleeping because of the thin walls. The room was clean and small. One day they installed shelves in our bathroom, without our notification, after which the room smelt of varnish for the remainder of the stay. The second room we stayed in was much better, it was 140 euro on the same floor, but was much bigger, and had two large windows overlooking the garden, we wish we had stayed in this room all week. If you like extra features in your hotel: gyms, spas etc than this isn't the hotel for you. If you are self-sufficient and don't require a lot of attention, than this hotel could be for you. It is good value for the money in a very very expensive city.Based on recommendations on this site, we took a taxi to the hotel upon arrival at CDG, it cost approx. 45 euros on a quiet Sunday morning with two suitcases. We took the RER on the return trip to the airport and was glad we didn't attempt it on our arrival, but is a good option when you get familiar with the metro system. It cost 16 euros and took approx. 1 hour.Thanks again to trip advisor for helping us select another great hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice overall impression Stayed at the Hotel de Varenne for 6 nights (March 5-11) with my wife and another couple. I liked the place quite a bit: GREAT location (close enough to things in general, but far enough away from hustle, bustle, and noise). Very good bakery 2 doors down, 2 grocery/convenience stores across the street - one operated by an extremely friendly guy who gave my wife a jar of nutella when she informed him that we were returning to the states the next day; a bnp paribas bank and atm on the same block (great for bank of america account holders - no atm transaction fees!).The only convenience we really lacked in the hotel was drawer space. Our room (#34, a double with a shower) didn't have any. Our friends stayed in room #44, which did. No complaints at all about the cleanliness, however.Madame Beatrix (who worked the front desk a lot) was really helpful, nice and friendly.All in all, we would stay there again, no question. You won't be disappointed if you go in expecting a good hotel and a good value. You will be disappointed if you go in expecting perfection.

<Author>DaPanda
<Content>Best Stay for the Money We stayed at the Varenne for a week at the end of January, having relied on reviews in Tripadvisor. As usual, this site did not let us down.We (2 of us) stayed in a superior room, which was more than ample. We happened to see inside a standard room while walking out, and that room size is above and beyond in size from what you find in Paris at a 3-star hotel.Our room was very clean, but do not expect the George V. Having the fridge in the room was a big plus. Staff is quiet but very helpful. Internet station (for a small fee based on 1 hour or 1/2 hour) also was convenient.The location is excellent as to having close access to the Metro and grocery and food shops. However, if you are carrying a lot of luggage, I do NOT recommend arriving at the hotel using anything other than a shuttle or taxi. The RER stations are a long walk if the weather is cold and some of the streets are narrow. Plus, the Varenne Metro stop is not great for transporting a large suitcase. What you spend in additional money is worth the convenience. Otherwise, if you are travelling light, the Metro or RER is fine. If you absolutely have to use the RER, use a station on the RER-B as your entry/exit point and taxi to/from the hotel.

Around the block from the Metro station 'Varenne' it is located in a very central, (right up the street from Musee Rodin) but quiet location with police and cameras everywhere as it is close to Embassy's. We felt safe getting off the Metro at anytime.After a long day in Paris, no worries, located right outside the hotel is everything you need and you won't have to walk far for an excellent meal no matter what your budget.From Orly to Hotel Varenne by Taxi: 22 EurosFrom Hotel Varenne to Orly Aiport: 40 EurosWith two people and luggage, this seemed like a bargain. You can take the Metro and transfer to a bus but in the end, the cost is probably equal to taking a taxi but without the headache.To get to Hotel Varenne from Charles de Gaulle:Take the RER 'Blue' Train and get off at St. Michel. Walk over to the RER 'Yellow' Train and go towards Versaille. A few stations down, exit at Invalides or transfer to the Metro 'light blue' light and get off at the next stop Varenne. Walk to Hotel Varenne from either the Varenne or Invalide Metro stop. (consult your own map- the hotel is very easy to find from the Invalide station).FYI- my most important advice....if you're flying out of Charles de Gaulle, before you get to the airport know which terminal you are flying out of (call the airline or go online!!) and give yourself PLENTY of time- 3-4 hours for international flights- I'm not kidding!! Good luck (especially if you're flying Air France or any of their partner airlines!!).Have fun (and skip Angelina's 'Famous' Hot Chocolate. Very, very sweet and thick. If you absolutely must try it, get one and share!)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Little Jewel of a Hotel I just took a business trip to Paris. I want to recommend Hotel Varenne as one of the classiest 3-star spots I know of. The room I was shown in was very clean, and smelled good. It was pleasantly warm (they have A/C and wall heaters), rather large, with plenty of space to accommodate a large suitcase. Nice, clean carpet, no dust on the furniture (Napoleon-style, I liked it). Overall it felt rich. The bathroom was spotless with marble-like amber-colored wall tiling, sparkling clean shower, a sink with a nice Corian top, heating rails for towels. The queen-sized bedding was firm but not too much, with a Treka springbox and mattress. Windows had double glazing, but even when I had them open (briefly, it's cold out there in January), I found traffic noise to be minimal: Bourgogne Street is a quiet one, and the room overlooks a fairly long courtyard. Wireless internet access is a pay-for system, but it's rather inexpensive. The hotel itself was well maintained and nicely decorated with wrought-iron handrails, and fine 19th-century prints. The owner, Mr. Pommier, is a mild-mannered gentleman in his early fifties. Always friendly, he was keen to help. The reception staff was also polite and helpful. I rate the hotel service as impeccable. On Mr. Pommier's recommendation, I had lunch nearby at a classy French restaurant named Chez Tante Marguerite. Truly delightful. The neighborhood is clean, quiet, and safe. The nearby Varenne Street is home to the French Prime Minister, the French Parliament, and several embassies: you can't walk 200 yards without seeing a cop. The St Germain des Pres district lies about 20 minutes away on foot. Overall, my experience with Hotel Varenne was very satisfying. Other TripAdvisor members also rate it highly, and I completely agree with them.

<Author>rlemon
<Content>Varenne: Family Hospitality The Hotel de Varenne is a bargain. It is located between the Invalides and the Place de Bourbon, and just a half block from the Rodin Museum. During the day, at least one family member is present and unfailingly helpful and courteous. The night staff were always multi-lingual and very competant and eager to please. The rooms were clean and effcient. Baths were refurbished. All public and private spaces were done in excellent taste. Breakfast was good, with fresh baguettes from a local baker. If you want a full breakfast, there are optional items at a modest cost. Each time I visit Paris, I try to stay in a different neighborhood. This time I chose the right bank near the Hotel des Invalides, where you can see the tomb of Napolean, part of the military museum complex. In the opposite direction you can take a rigorous 10 minute walk to the Musee' d'Orsay and the St. Germain neighborhood, with its art galleries and elegant shops. Five minutes from the hotel you are standing on the esplanade above the Seine River.In the hotel, internet service is free if you have your own computer. The building is hot. Otherwise, be prepared to pay six Euros an hour to buy a card and use their one station. There are no internet cafes in the area, so the options are nil; this was my only complaint.This hotel is among the Top 10 among TripAdvisor Paris hotels, and the lowest priced of that group. Thanks to TripAdvisor for the tip and this lucky find.

<Content>Nice and Quiet We stayed at Hotel de Varenne over the Thanksgiving holiday. It was quiet, clean, nicely if modestly decorated, and comfortable for a hotel in this price range. <Author>Bucknut_Girl
<Content>Homey, Friendly Staff, and Great Location We booked the Hotel de Varenne for 9 nights over the Christmas holiday based on Tripadvisor reviews, and we were not disappointed. Those of you who prefer to pay $300-$500 per night for a large chain with spa etc, may not find the homey atmosphere and quiet location your thing, but we loved it. The area is very safe and quiet, but right in the middle of all the fun areas you'll want to go. We took the RER from the airport and transferred to the C-line, so it couldn't have been easier to get to the hotel from the Invalides metro stop. As others have mentioned, there are great bakeries, produce stands, and markets on the street to grab anything you need to stock your hotel fridge. We enjoyed breakfast at the hotel (the traditional French nosh of baked goods and coffee), but anyone who is looking for a big American breakfast will need to get used to the grocery store. The staff at the hotel were very helpful and polite. The hotel owner, Jean Marc Pommier, went so far as to bake us bread one night when all the bakeries on our street were closed over the Christmas holiday! We were a little intimidated because we didn't speak much French, but as long as you practice some general niceties and try a little French, the locals are wonderful. Just note that they work a 35 hour wk, but when they work, they are extremely busy. They like to be efficient and understandably will get irritated if you dawdle and hold up service for other customers (see complaint in earlier review).As for the room, we had a nice size bedroom and bathroom by Europen standards. The beds leave you a little stiff in the morning, but are probably about the best we've had in our visits to Europe. Comments about cleanliness are correct, as this is one of the cleanest places around and recently renovated. (Just keep in mind to dodge the doggie droppings while out walking though.) The rooms are fairly quiet inside, and we had a view of the top of the Eiffel tower and the courtyard which was nice. We have definitely been recommending the Hotel de Varenne to friends and family and hope to come back soon!

<Author>Nashville1
<Content>Generally Good Hotel We spent 4 nights at the Hotel Varenne. Our rooms were smallish but well furnished and clean. The location is great, on a fairly quiet street and a 2 block walk to the Varenne metro station. Although the hotel advertises it is air conditioned, we found that the system had been turned off for the winter. It was unseasonably warm so we had to open the windows and endure the noise. Getting around is easy if you use the metro or walk. Getting a cab is harder--there are no cab stands nearby and few cabs frequent the area. If the hotel calls a cab, the meter starts when the cab leaves the stand--expect a 5-9 euro add on to the fare because of that. I would also echo the comment made in an earlier review--there is a potential fire safety issue with only one central open staircase and no fire doors. If the staircase was blocked there is no other exit from the top floors.

One note that I will make, and I found this at all our stops in large cities in Europe, parking is expensive and inconvenient. If I do it again, I will not drive into Paris but instead take a train.

<Author>DaProf
<Content>Lovely stay This is a small Left Bank hotel that feels more like a large bed and breakfast. Our window actually opened, and it looked out on the pleasant courtyard at the off-street hotel entrance. The hotel is walking distance from the Seine, the Place de la Concorde, Boulevard St. Germain, Rodin Museum and Orsay Museum. Metro stops are omnipresent and get you anywhere quickly and cheaply. Our room was comparatively spacious (rooms are smaller in Europe than the USA) and very quiet. I have never, anywhere, been in a better-maintained hotel. The rooms, indeed the entire premise, are spotless and bright. They must scour the bathroom tile grout with toothbrushes. I am sure this is the only place in the world where one sees the hotel manager himself on a ladder cleaning and polishing the outside lighting fixtures. The staff was quite pleasant, save a glitch with a night clerk over purchase of Internet time.Breakfast (only) consisting of croissants, danish and coffee is available in the small dining area or your room for 10E, more for cooked items. But, there is better in the area. There is nothing, but nothing on earth, so wonderful as fresh-baked French bread and pastry in Paris. In our week at the Varenne, we usually ate breakfast from the Patisserie Besneir a few doors away. Unbelievable. We often prepared a takeaway picnic lunch or dinner from the same place, getting some fresh fruit, cheese and drinks from the Proxi mini market across the street. There are many small restaurants in the immediate area and sidewalk caf茅 upon sidewalk caf茅 are within walking distance.Our only actual bad experience in Paris was getting a purse pick-pocketed at the Orsay Museum. While we had heard that this kind of crime is common there, it is much worse than we had anticipated and the French police seem to do little about it. Pickpockets swarm in public places, especially among tourists. There are also petty thieves on one pretty quickly when attempting the Metro ticket machines or staring at a street map. This is an issue about which to be concerned when considering a Paris visit.The Hotel de Varenne is a lovely, unpretentious, beautifully maintained little hotel with reasonable rates. If you prefer the full-service George V sort of thing, go to the Right Bank and spend five or six times more. We enjoyed our stay at the Varenne and would happily stay again.

<Author>CHerPig
<Content>Excellent boutique hotel Hotel Varenne was our 1st experience in Paris. Very happy with room size and extreme cleanliness. Staff was very pleasant and efficient. We did not try breakfast @ hotel. Generously sized shampoo and soap amenities, PLUS washcoths! Most importantly--area is EXTREMELY safe! Located near international embassies. We preferred to walk to the Invalides metro instead. Invalides is equally close, but it provides more selection of metro lines. We found Paris's metro to be EXCELLENT--clean, safe, and efficient. Absolutely no need to use rental car or taxis! Strongly suggest buying the orange pass. Valid for 1 week  includes unlimited metro/bus travel...a terrific investment even if used only 4 days.We highly recommend the Hotel Varenne and will certainly stay there again!

<Author>Boutique_Freak
<Content>A Nice Little Hotel The first thing we noticed about the de Varenne is its location. Everything is close by -- Les Invalides, The Rodin Museum, the Eiffel Tower. It is also close to the little things a traveler might need -- pharmacy, cash machine and terrific little bread and pastry shops. The street is quiet and makes for a nice respite in the middle of a big city.You enter the de Varenne through a cute little courtyard garden. The indoor public spaces are minimal. There is a tiny lobby and a nice little breakfast room with about 8 tables. Our welcome was warm, but not exceptional. We spoke mostly French, but the staff were quite competent in English. The breakfast was a bit too American style for our tastes, but served by a lovely woman who catered to every whim.The rooms at the de Varenne are nice. They are small but well-furnished with nice creature comforts like flat-screen TVs. Ours (#18) looked out over the back of the entry courtyard for a fantastic view. Double-paned windows kept everything nice and quiet. Our bathroom was a bit plain, but fitted with top-of-the line taps. Everything was comfortable and clean.Overall, the Hotel de Varenne is a nice place to stay. It blends location and good amenities with decent (but not exceptional) service. We would -- and probably will -- stay there again.
